        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513372369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer637318855426682929">There is so much to love about this book. <br/><br/>Scarlett is a fabulous heroine. She is funny, smart (loves all the same books I do!) and level headed. Even though she definitely had three love interests, she wasn't that dithering heroine that is leading everyone on, and is in love with whoever she is with at the moment. I have to say this was one of the first love triangles (squares?) where I didn't hate how the heroine handled everything. She was honest with herself and (with one notable exception) h</span>
  <span id="freeText637318855426682929" style="display:none">There is so much to love about this book. <br><br>Scarlett is a fabulous heroine. She is funny, smart (loves all the same books I do!) and level headed. Even though she definitely had three love interests, she wasn't that dithering heroine that is leading everyone on, and is in love with whoever she is with at the moment. I have to say this was one of the first love triangles (squares?) where I didn't hate how the heroine handled everything. She was honest with herself and (with one notable exception) honest with all the guys involved. <br><br>Oh, and those boys....yummy. I always have a favorite in these scenarios . I'm never confused about who I want the heroine to chose, but this time, two of the three completely captured my heart. (The third was great too, but I just knew he wasn't going to work out) I'm still totally torn about who I'm rooting for. (Maybe they can share? :) <br><br>First she meets Ash. Delicious surfer man-whore. Usually this type turns me off, but oh my. I was completely choked up after one of their first real conversations. He is so much more than he looks like on the surface. ..not that his surface isn't tempting. <br><br><a href="http://s50.photobucket.com/albums/f339/vikkimathews/?action=view&amp;current=b7e2b7cb0e04155e453fbe094d3a9c13.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380406198i/792202.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Then she meets Dylan. All American, Abercrombie hot, loves books, works hard, all around total package.<br><br><a href="http://s50.photobucket.com/albums/f339/vikkimathews/?action=view&amp;current=3b4da0807c41328ccc2f6f83b131125c.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380406198i/792203.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And final bad boy, tattooed and pierced rocker Mason. *swoon* love Mason from head to toe, and everything in between.<br><br><a href="http://s50.photobucket.com/albums/f339/vikkimathews/?action=view&amp;current=73f92b58785fb5248c320efd745353a7.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380406198i/792204._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Sheltered Scarlett handles all three (some more than others) with amazing grace, all with the help of one of my favorite best friend characters of all time, Evie. <br><br>Scattered throughout the book were great references to some of my favorite books of the last few years, which made everything all that much more awesome. Fifty Shades, Taking Chances, Runing me, Knight, and Beautiful disaster all get some play. <br><br>I feel like I'm not doing it justice. I laughed, I cried, I fell in love (twice). I swooned, I got mad, I got my heartbroken. I loved every word, and wouldn't change a single thing. <br><br>The ending...well, it's not exactly a cliffhanger....but it definitely lets you know that while things got wrapped up in book one, that's not the end of the story by a long shot. <br><br>I cannot wait for book two. <br><br>One of the best new YA books I've read. Try it out, you won't be disappointed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="637318855426682929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474174364" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9675790445692519301">I was given an ARC for an honest review. <br/><br/>This was a great debut novel that had my heart pounding at the end. Scarlett is a young, sheltered girl on a journey to become a woman. She meets three hot guys along the way and has to choose which is best for her. The first half, we get to know Scarlett and she made some choices that left me frazzled but she was always likeable. Although she is inexperienced she isn't a pushover. I loved her interactions with her best friend Evie. Their interactions had</span>
  <span id="freeText9675790445692519301" style="display:none">I was given an ARC for an honest review. <br /><br />This was a great debut novel that had my heart pounding at the end. Scarlett is a young, sheltered girl on a journey to become a woman. She meets three hot guys along the way and has to choose which is best for her. The first half, we get to know Scarlett and she made some choices that left me frazzled but she was always likeable. Although she is inexperienced she isn't a pushover. I loved her interactions with her best friend Evie. Their interactions had me smiling at some of the things they talked about. We see Scarlett start to feel things she's always read about but never experienced. Some choices are made from lack of experience and others are made from pure want. <br /><br />The second half of the book really took off and I had no idea who she would choose. The ending left me absolutely riveted! Although my favorite didn't get the girl, I love books that give me that ache in my chest and this one did that for me. I love to make that connection to my book characters where I feel their "pain" and kudos to Erin Noelle for upsetting me!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9675790445692519301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5609514903337624530" style="display:none">I was given an ARC for an honest review &amp; thats just what I intend to do because regardless of how much I love an author its the book that I am reviewing and not the author.<br />That being said...This book far exceeded my expectations from a first time author in this genre and recommended read for those who enjoy Mature YA. <br />This is a story of a young woman who is beginning her first year at college with her BFF &amp; gettin out from under her parents thumb. She is new to just about every life experience a teenager typically goes through and embarks on a journey of self discovery, heartache, loss and love. The author did an amazing job with creating characters that you can feel and at most times even relate to. Sure, there were times when I was rolling my eyes because all the boys would just instantly fall all over themselves for our heroine but the yummy main male characters make up for it **swoon** You will laugh, you will cry and you will want to shake the crap out of something at times but it all comes together at the end and the author even gives us a sweet little treat (epilogue).</span>

<div id="review_473888915" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473888915" />
    <a title="Kirsty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10389044-kirsty"><img alt="Kirsty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409522343p2/10389044.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473888915?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirsty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirsty" href="/user/show/10389044-kirsty">Kirsty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Molly McAdams</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10389044-kirsty?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10389044-kirsty?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473888915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12279365474318249299">*I was provided an ARC by the author in turn for an honest review.*<br/><br/>3.5 stars<br/><br/>For me this book wasn't a 3.5 stars because it was a bad story, or because the writing was awful - the kind of story just purely isn't for me. I have read Taking Chances, From Ashes and now Metamorphosis and they all have a huge similarity that I have now learnt I don't particularly like - A young, naive, virginal girl who has finally broken free from a sheltered life and is thrown in to the craziness that is college, wi</span>
  <span id="freeText12279365474318249299" style="display:none">*I was provided an ARC by the author in turn for an honest review.*<br /><br />3.5 stars<br /><br />For me this book wasn't a 3.5 stars because it was a bad story, or because the writing was awful - the kind of story just purely isn't for me. I have read Taking Chances, From Ashes and now Metamorphosis and they all have a huge similarity that I have now learnt I don't particularly like - A young, naive, virginal girl who has finally broken free from a sheltered life and is thrown in to the craziness that is college, with boys throwing themselves at her.<br /><br />In Metamorphosis, when Scarlett MacGregor starts college, along with her best friend Evie, she is ready to experience everything she has been missing out on - boys, parties, drinking, boys, making her own decisions, and oh yeah boys! The minute she comes in contact with certain boys, three in particular, it's like she is a walking goddess and they can't keep their eyes off her. Cue the pissing contest and endless 'will she' 'won't she' questions regarding the three boys. <br /><br />We have Ash the bad boy womanizer, Dylan the preppy school boy and Mason the sexy bad boy rockstar. One of each of our favourite types of Book Boyfriend. Scarlett turns into an insta-whore near enough over night, minus the sex, and goes from one boy to the next. She doesn't necessarily make the best decisions but since she has been sheltered for so long she finds it hard to slow down and contentrate on just one boy.<br />I won't give any clue's to who Scarlett ends up with in the end but I will just say - Team Ash all the way! <br /><br />There were ALOT of references to other books in Metamorphosis. Ruining Me by Nicole Reed and Taking Chances by Molly McAdams were just two of the few. I am all for references in books, quite often it makes me smile or laugh out loud, especially if I have read the book! Unfortunately, it didn't work so much for me in this book, I just found it a little bit too much.<br /><br />Like I said in the beginning, this wasn't a bad book at all it's just that this 'type' doesn't necessarily work for me. I can just about deal with love triangles, let alone love squares. If you are a particular fan of Molly McAdams books though, I highly recommend you reading Metamorphosis.<br />Saying all that though, I am looking forward to the next book in the series to see who exactly gets their HAE and who with.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12279365474318249299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_548540513" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/548540513" />
    <a title="Sarah Bervoets" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2525330-sarah-bervoets"><img alt="Sarah Bervoets" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520680885p2/2525330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/548540513?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Bervoets" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Bervoets" href="/user/show/2525330-sarah-bervoets">Sarah Bervoets</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2525330-sarah-bervoets?shelf=a-z-book-challenge">a-z-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2525330-sarah-bervoets?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer548540513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7844188511006856280">I really wanted to hate this book. <br/>I was all set on giving it one star.<br/>But literally on the <b>LAST</b> page. It kind of won me over. <br/>...kind of <br/>I'm actually confused as hell right now, cause I honestly have no idea what I just read. <br/>I mean what exactly was the book about in the end? <br/>It began being about freedom and getting away from her parents. <br/>Then it was her friendship with Evie, next came all the boys, and then it all just abruptly halted and all of a sudden it was about her finding herself. <br/>But h</span>
  <span id="freeText7844188511006856280" style="display:none">I really wanted to hate this book. <br>I was all set on giving it one star.<br>But literally on the <b>LAST</b> page. It kind of won me over. <br>...kind of <br>I'm actually confused as hell right now, cause I honestly have no idea what I just read. <br>I mean what exactly was the book about in the end? <br>It began being about freedom and getting away from her parents. <br>Then it was her friendship with Evie, next came all the boys, and then it all just abruptly halted and all of a sudden it was about her finding herself. <br>But her "metamorphosis" was literally in about the last 20 pages of the book. <br>I have a thing for last lines. I love when the last line of a book has a significant meaning to the story.<br>And that is the ONLY reason this book is getting ANY stars. <br><br><b>“And I only hope you still want me to be the Angel to your Rat.” I turned up my nose just slightly when I said his nickname. <br>“All along I was wearing the wrong wings.” <br>Mason slowly made his way towards me and stepped up onto the stage. I didn’t move. He looked down at me and seared me with his intense stare. <br>“Don’t you ever fly away again, Angel. I swear I’ll have your wings clipped.” Then he picked me up into his arms and crushed me against his body. <br>“I’ve missed you so much, Angel. I love you.”<br> “I love you too, Rat boy. I love you, too.”</b><br><br>That was all beautiful and awesome, don't get me wrong.<br>But here's the thing I'm so confused about:<br>The book is called <i>Metamorphosis</i>. <br>She has the Butterfly <i>Ash</i> drew tattooed on her calf.<br>Ash was the one who gave her the nickname Butterfly.... <br>She claimed to love Ash for pretty much the entire book and yet, at the last second.... she ends up with Mason. <br>For a book so obsessed with books it really messed up the dynamic there. <br>Everyone knows that the first guy the girl meets is the one she ultimately ends up with. <br>Even in books with love triangles or whatever the hell this book had, the reader always knows who will win in the end. And yet, in this book, it was just a complete 180. <br>Like seriously, what the hell just happened? <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380411518ra/808465.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I realize there <i>might</i> be another book in this series but even so, I don't understand how this book could end up like that. The worst is when you have a favorite guy out of the two, and the main character loves them both, it just makes you want to punch them in the face and that is what I wanted to do more than once when reading this. <br><br>It also annoyed me how much they talked about books. <br>I didn't mind the mention of Taking Chances or Beautiful Disaster, that was cool.<br>It annoyed me when they said stuff like:<br><b>"...ya’ll will end up together with a magical, fairy-tale, happily-ever-after. But you know as well as I do that it takes a bunch of other bullshit in between to get that point - a bunch of unnecessary angst, some preventable misunderstandings, and you both need to make some ill-advised and senseless decisions."</b><br>That really annoyed me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/585653.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But the thing that pissed me off most about this entire book was all the "Insta-Love" <br><b>Oh.My.Word.</b> <br>It is the worst when two characters have known each other all of two minutes and are already calling each other soul-mates. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380407733ra/796763.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It makes me want to punch someone. <br>I can understand Insta-Lust, because obviously you can look at someone and instantly be attracted to them. But you cannot look at someone and instantly KNOW you love them, instantly KNOW you have a connection with that person even though all you've done is had some steamy eye contact.<br>Lust happens immediately, granted. Feelings, DON'T! <br>And in this book the author did that with not only ONE but all THREE main guys. <br>It was like they met Scarlett and the next minute they were in love with her. It was infuriating.<br><br><b>"I feel this strange connection to you."</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/551191.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not to mention I hate that she had such a sheltered life and then as soon as she gets her freedom it automatically has to be all about boys, not even remotely about anything else.<br>I don’t understand that. <br><br>Even though I don't like who she ended up with, I'm not really all that upset about it. <br>And it was kind of like every guy in the book was the same. Ladies man who was actually a closet softie. <br>The characters weren't really definable as their own. <br>I also didn't cry when Evie died. I knew it was coming. It just didn't evoke any strong emotions in me other than irritation at being so predictable. <br>I really wanted this book to be better.<br>I was really disappointed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7844188511006856280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_531793754" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/531793754" />
    <a title="♥ Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13161862-sarah"><img alt="♥ Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455167556p2/13161862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/531793754?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ Sarah" href="/user/show/13161862-sarah">♥ Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13161862-sarah?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer531793754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3906093226217665552">I almost DNF. <br/><br/>Look, I think BBB just like the rest of you. And, despite my inner feminist, I loved Travis from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11505797.Beautiful_Disaster__Beautiful___1_' title='Beautiful Disaster (Beautiful, #1) by Jamie McGuire' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beautiful Disaster</a>. And, I have a thing for the underdog & hot rockers, so naturally, I was rooting for Rhys, in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17260623.Ruining_Me__Ruining___1_' title='Ruining Me (Ruining, #1) by Nicole Reed' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ruining Me</a>. Alanis Morissette- You Oughta Know got me through some heartbreaking break-ups; I know anger, pain, lust, heartbreak, sexual tension, and boys. I love stories with witty banter, dripping with sarcasm, with a touch of irony, and big crazy twists. <br/><br/>And yet, <i>Metamorph</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3906093226217665552" style="display:none">I almost DNF. <br /><br />Look, I think BBB just like the rest of you. And, despite my inner feminist, I loved Travis from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11505797.Beautiful_Disaster__Beautiful___1_" title="Beautiful Disaster (Beautiful, #1) by Jamie McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">Beautiful Disaster</a>. And, I have a thing for the underdog &amp; hot rockers, so naturally, I was rooting for Rhys, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17260623.Ruining_Me__Ruining___1_" title="Ruining Me (Ruining, #1) by Nicole Reed" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruining Me</a>. Alanis Morissette- You Oughta Know got me through some heartbreaking break-ups; I know anger, pain, lust, heartbreak, sexual tension, and boys. I love stories with witty banter, dripping with sarcasm, with a touch of irony, and big crazy twists. <br /><br />And yet, <i>Metamorphosis</i> makes a joke of all of those things I love. <br />I kept thinking to myself: <b>IS THIS A PARODY OR A SATIRE?</b> <br /><br />PLEASE TELL ME THIS WAS SOME KIND OF A JOKE...? <br /><br />** <br /><br />Scarlet is free now that she is 18 years old. She moved out of her "crazy" overprotective, controlling parents' home, to start fresh in college, with her best friend Evie. She's an 18 year old virgin that's never been kissed, never been on a date, never had ONE guy FRIEND in her life before, attended an all girls high school, never wore nail polish, never stepped foot inside a HAIR SALON!!!! WTF? And her explanation? "My parents were just over protective." [...] <br /><br />OK, BUT THAT'S NOT ALL, FOLKS.<br /><br />She gets herself a make-over, and stocks up on her "sexy" lingerie, because well, she needs to give up her V-card now, right? She's in college! <br /><br />She meets not 1, or 2, but wait for it...THREE (for lack of a better word) <i>retarded</i> guys. One of the guy's nickname is "RAT." Enough said. <br /><br />I don't even want to mention ASH. He's creepy, and not hot at all. The "excuse" he gives Scarlet made me want to puke and roll my eyes up to heaven. Really dude? Was that the best ya got? Ultimately, he's a "play boy" and you know how <i>that</i> goes. Nothing unique, or unpredictable happens.<br /><br />Except, well, the *TWIST* - Oh goodie! <br /><br />The author must've decided she wanted to make Scar a "deep" character that "overcame" some sort of personal tragedy, or something ridiculous, because she decides to KILL OFF a character! For no reason! Just for the sake of drama... <br /><br />Words fail me.<br /><br />...<br />...<br />...<br /><br /><br />The whole thing was just bizarre... I couldn't relate to any of the characters. The story telling was off, too. Most of it was all telling, rather than showing. And there were one too many 'steamy' scenes, just for the sake of it. <br /><br />*NOTE: this was my own personal opinion of the book. Just because I didn't like it, doesn't mean the book sucks, or that the next reader won't love it. Everyone's different. And it's nothing personal, but sometimes, people just have different opinions. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3906093226217665552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sXIWyCA882wh+2vDIIsb+nzOmHVEHDU+vT/CuYo12YIKlnxLs4LzeC3uODK3Z9uht92Qae1kU0rCQ5k6kd4JZA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5QpBOfCyWwfsMfn0JZbLgjJ92r0x192SNofiK2hCveJe7iu6YwxbE+AkqgWyegvZ+W7SoZivu+ZJ+7moc6ltBA==')})
  }
//]]>

He\'s a f*cking train wreck. But a precious train wreck. And I can\'t help myself: I love the sh*t out of him, even though I hate him. Even though I don\'t. Don\'t ask. It\'s complicated. \n\nBut he\'s also a rock star and now, so am I. The Goddess of Guitar, I guess. All I really want is to make music and see how hard it is to fall in love with a man who\'s a devil at heart but sings like an angel. \n\nIf I\'m going to lay my heart on the line again though, I deserve a real chance. I won\'t be a pawn in this f*cking game any longer. \n\nI don\'t care how dangerous the stakes are anymore. I\'m taking charge of my own destiny, like I should\'ve all along. I won\'t have the wool pulled over my eyes and I won\'t bend over for fate. Get ready, b*tches, because Naomi Knox is coming for you. \n\nMature - Ages 18 and Up. <span id="freeTextContainer15138491789644019774">Erin Noelle is a Texas native, where she lives with her husband, two daughters, and three fur babies. When she's not reading or writing romance novels, she enjoys winning at cards and board games, awkward people-watching in public places, and doing cartwheels at the most random times.   <span id="freeText15138491789644019774" style="display:none">Erin Noelle is a Texas native, where she lives with her husband, two daughters, and three fur babies. When she's not reading or writing romance novels, she enjoys winning at cards and board games, awkward people-watching in public places, and doing cartwheels at the most random times. She's usually barefoot, is never without a song in her head, and currently holds the title of World's Best Procrastinator.<br />Her titles published include the Book Boyfriend Series, Dusk 'Til Dawn Series, Luminous Duet, Fire on the Mountain series, and numerous standalone books that range from New Adult to Contemporary romance. Her books have been a part of the USA Today Bestselling list as well as the Amazon and Barnes &amp; Noble overall Top 100. You can follow her on Facebook @ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/erin.noelle.98">www.facebook.com/erin.noelle.98</a>, her blog @ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.erinnoelleauthor.com">www.erinnoelleauthor.com</a>, on Twitter @authorenoelle, and on Instagram @erinnoelleauthor. </span>
